import math

def calculate_distance(x1, y1, x2, y2):
    return math.sqrt((x2 - x1) ** 2 + (y2 - y1) ** 2)

def calculate_area(radius):
    return math.pi * (radius ** 2)

class Geometry:
    def __init__(self, side_length):
        self.side_length = side_length

    def calculate_perimeter(self):
        return self.side_length * 4

    def calculate_area(self):
        return self.side_length ** 2

import math

def calculate_distance(x1, y1, x2, y2):
    """
    Calculate the Euclidean distance between two points.

    Args:
        x1 (float): The x-coordinate of the first point.
        y1 (float): The y-coordinate of the first point.
        x2 (float): The x-coordinate of the second point.
        y2 (float): The y-coordinate of the second point.

    Returns:
        float: The Euclidean distance between the two points.
    """
    return math.sqrt((x2 - x1) ** 2 + (y2 - y1) ** 2)

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return math.pi * (radius ** 2)

class Geometry:
    """
    A class representing geometric shapes.

    Attributes:
        side_length (float): The length of the side of the shape.
    """

    def __init__(self, side_length):
        """
        Initialize the Geometry class.

        Args:
            side_length (float): The length of the side of the shape.
        """
        self.side_length = side_length

    def calculate_perimeter(self):
        """
        Calculate the perimeter of a square.

        Returns:
            float: The perimeter of the square.
        """
        return self.side_length * 4

    def calculate_area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of a square.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the square.
        """
        return self.side_length ** 2

# math_ops.py
import math

def add(a, b):
    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number to add.
        b (int or float): The second number to add.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
        >>> add(2.5, 3.7)
        6.2
    """
    return a + b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Multiplies two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number to multiply.
        b (int or float): The second number to multiply.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(2, 3)
        6
        >>> multiply(2.5, 3.7)
        9.25
    """
    return a * b

# stats_ops.py
import statistics

def calculate_mean(numbers):
    """
    Calculates the mean of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        float: The mean of the numbers.

    Examples:
        >>> calculate_mean([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])
        3.0
    """
    return statistics.mean(numbers)

def calculate_median(numbers):
    """
    Calculates the median of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        float: The median of the numbers.

    Examples:
        >>> calculate_median([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])
        3
    """
    return statistics.median(numbers)

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Returns the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(4, 5)
        20
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Returns the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ZeroDivisionError: If b is zero.

    Examples:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5
    """
    return a / b

import math

def add(a, b):
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b

def calculate_area(radius):
    return math.pi * radius ** 2

def calculate_circumference(radius):
    return 2 * math.pi * radius

import math

def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Returns the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Returns the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If the divisor is zero.
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Returns the area of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (int or float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        int or float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return math.pi * radius ** 2

def calculate_circumference(radius):
    """
    Returns the circumference of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (int or float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        int or float: The circumference of the circle.
    """
    return 2 * math.pi * radius

# python module: mathematics.py
def add(a, b):
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return a / b

# python module: statistics.py
def calculate_mean(numbers):
    return sum(numbers) / len(numbers)

def calculate_median(numbers):
    numbers.sort()
    mid = len(numbers) // 2
    return numbers[mid] if len(numbers) % 2!= 0 else (numbers[mid - 1] + numbers[mid]) / 2

# python module: mathematics.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference between two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference between a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Returns the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(4, 5)
        20
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Returns the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If the divisor is zero.

    Examples:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return a / b

# python module: statistics.py
def calculate_mean(numbers):
    """
    Returns the arithmetic mean of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        float: The arithmetic mean of the numbers.

    Examples:
        >>> calculate_mean([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])
        3
    """
    return sum(numbers) / len(numbers)

def calculate_median(numbers):
    """
    Returns the median of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        float: The median of the numbers.

    Examples:
        >>> calculate_median([1, 3, 5])
        3
        >>> calculate_median([1, 2, 3, 4])
        2.5
    """
    numbers.sort()
    mid = len(numbers) // 2
    return numbers[mid] if len(numbers) % 2!= 0 else (numbers[mid - 1] + numbers[mid]) / 2

"""
my_module.py
------------

This module provides various utility functions for mathematical operations.
"""

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """Return the sum of two numbers."""
    return a + b

def multiply_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """Return the product of two numbers."""
    return a * b

def calculate_area(radius: float) -> float:
    """Return the area of a circle given its radius."""
    return 3.14 * radius ** 2

"""
another_module.py
-----------------

This module provides a function to check if a number is prime.
"""

def is_prime(n: int) -> bool:
    """Return True if the number is prime, False otherwise."""
    if n <= 1:
        return False
    if n == 2:
        return True
    if n % 2 == 0:
        return False
    max_divisor = int(n**0.5) + 1
    for d in range(3, max_divisor, 2):
        if n % d == 0:
            return False
    return True

# my_module.py
"""
my_module.py
------------

This module provides various utility functions for mathematical operations.

Classes:
    None

Functions:
    add_numbers(a, b)
        Return the sum of two numbers.

    multiply_numbers(a, b)
        Return the product of two numbers.

    calculate_area(radius)
        Return the area of a circle given its radius.
"""

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Return the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def multiply_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Return the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The product of a and b.
    """
    return a * b

def calculate_area(radius: float) -> float:
    """
    Return the area of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return 3.14 * radius ** 2


# another_module.py
"""
another_module.py
-----------------

This module provides a function to check if a number is prime.

Classes:
    None

Functions:
    is_prime(n)
        Return True if the number is prime, False otherwise.
"""

def is_prime(n: int) -> bool:
    """
    Return True if the number is prime, False otherwise.

    Args:
        n (int): The number to check.

    Returns:
        bool: True if the number is prime, False otherwise.
    """
    if n <= 1:
        return False
    if n == 2:
        return True
    if n % 2 == 0:
        return False
    max_divisor = int(n**0.5) + 1
    for d in range(3, max_divisor, 2):
        if n % d == 0:
            return False
    return True

        Adds two numbers.
        
        Args:

        b (int): The second number.
        
        Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.

        """
        Subtracts two numbers.
        
        Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.
        
        Returns:
        int: The difference of a and b.

module2.py:
"""
Module for greeting and farewell messages.
"""

def greet(name):
    """
    Prints a personalized greeting message.
    
    Args:
    name (str): The name of the person to greet.
    
    Returns:
    None
    """
    print(f"Hello, {name}!")

def farewell(name):
    """
    Prints a personalized farewell message.
    
    Args:
    name (str): The name of the person to bid farewell.
    
    Returns:
    None
    """
    print(f"Goodbye, {name}!")

# silly_module.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Adds two numbers together. Because math.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.

    Example:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Subtracts one number from another. Also math.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The difference of a and b.

    Example:
        >>> subtract(5, 2)
        3
    """
    return a - b


# another_silly_module.py
def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Multiplies two numbers together. Yep, more math.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The product of a and b.

    Example:
        >>> multiply(4, 5)
        20
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Divides one number by another. But don't try to divide by zero, that's just silly.

    Args:
        a (int): The dividend.
        b (int): The divisor.

    Returns:
        float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If b is zero.

    Example:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5.0
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Don't be silly, can't divide by zero!")
    return a / b

# This is a sample module with functions to demonstrate docstring generation
# We will use the following code as an example
# Define a module named 'math_utils' with two functions: 'add_numbers' and 'multiply_numbers'
# Also, define a class named 'MathOperations' with methods 'add' and 'multiply'

def add_numbers(a, b):
    """Add two numbers."""
    return a + b

def multiply_numbers(a, b):
    """Multiply two numbers."""
    return a * b

class MathOperations:
    def add(self, a, b):
        """Add two numbers."""
        return a + b

    def multiply(self, a, b):
        """Multiply two numbers."""
        return a * b

def main():
    math_ops = MathOperations()
    print(math_ops.add(5, 3))
    print(math_ops.multiply(5, 3))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

"""
math_utils Module
================

This module provides basic mathematical operations.

Functions
---------
add_numbers(a, b)
    Add two numbers.
multiply_numbers(a, b)
    Multiply two numbers.

Classes
-------
MathOperations
    A class for mathematical operations.

    Methods
    -------
    add(a, b)
        Add two numbers.
    multiply(a, b)
        Multiply two numbers.
"""

def add_numbers(a, b):
    """
    Add two numbers.

    Parameters
    ----------
    a : int
        The first number.
    b : int
        The second number.

    Returns
    -------
    int
        The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def multiply_numbers(a, b):
    """
    Multiply two numbers.

    Parameters
    ----------
    a : int
        The first number.
    b : int
        The second number.

    Returns
    -------
    int
        The product of a and b.
    """
    return a * b

class MathOperations:
    """
    A class for mathematical operations.

    Methods
    -------
    add(a, b)
        Add two numbers.
    multiply(a, b)
        Multiply two numbers.
    """

    def add(self, a, b):
        """
        Add two numbers.

        Parameters
        ----------
        a : int
            The first number.
        b : int
            The second number.

        Returns
        -------
        int
            The sum of a and b.
        """
        return a + b

    def multiply(self, a, b):
        """
        Multiply two numbers.

        Parameters
        ----------
        a : int
            The first number.
        b : int
            The second number.

        Returns
        -------
        int
            The product of a and b.
        """
        return a * b

def main():
    """
    The main function to demonstrate the usage of MathOperations class.
    """
    math_ops = MathOperations()
    print(math_ops.add(5, 3))
    print(math_ops.multiply(5, 3))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

# mathematics.py
"""
This module contains mathematical functions.

Functions:
    calculate_area(radius): Calculates the area of a circle.
    calculate_circumference(radius): Calculates the circumference of a circle.
"""

import math

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculates the area of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return math.pi * (radius ** 2)

def calculate_circumference(radius):
    """
    Calculates the circumference of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The circumference of the circle.
    """
    return 2 * math.pi * radius


# statistics.py
"""
This module contains statistical functions.

Functions:
    calculate_mean(data): Calculates the mean of a dataset.
    calculate_median(data): Calculates the median of a dataset.
"""

import statistics

def calculate_mean(data):
    """
    Calculates the mean of a dataset.

    Args:
        data (list): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        float: The mean of the dataset.
    """
    return statistics.mean(data)

def calculate_median(data):
    """
    Calculates the median of a dataset.

    Args:
        data (list): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        float: The median of the dataset.
    """
    return statistics.median(data)

from math import pi

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return pi * radius ** 2

def calculate_circumference(radius):
    """
    Calculate the circumference of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The circumference of the circle.
    """
    return 2 * pi * radius

class Circle:
    """
    A class representing a circle.

    Attributes:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.
    """

    def __init__(self, radius):
        """
        Initialize a Circle object.

        Args:
            radius (float): The radius of the circle.
        """
        self.radius = radius

    def calculate_area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def calculate_circumference(self):
        """
        Calculate the circumference of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The circumference of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_circumference(self.radius)

# my_module.py
def add_numbers(a, b):
    return a + b

        """

        Args:
            num1 (int): The first number.
            num2 (int): The second number.

        self.num1 = num1
        self.num2 = num2

    def multiply(self):
        """
        Multiplies the two numbers together.

        Returns:
            int: The product of num1 and num2.
        """
        return self.num1 * self.num2

        """
        Divides the first number by the second number.

        Returns:
            float: The quotient of num1 and num2.

            ValueError: If num2 is zero.

    return a + b

    return a * b

# statistics.py
import math

def calculate_mean(numbers):
    return sum(numbers) / len(numbers)

def calculate_median(numbers):
    numbers.sort()
    n = len(numbers)
    if n % 2 == 0:
        return (numbers[n // 2 - 1] + numbers[n // 2]) / 2
    else:
        return numbers[n // 2]

def calculate_standard_deviation(numbers):
    mean = calculate_mean(numbers)
    variance = sum((x - mean) ** 2 for x in numbers) / len(numbers)
    return math.sqrt(variance)

# main.py
import math_operations
import statistics

def main():
    numbers = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]
    mean = statistics.calculate_mean(numbers)
    median = statistics.calculate_median(numbers)
    std_dev = statistics.calculate_standard_deviation(numbers)
    print(f"Mean: {mean}, Median: {median}, Standard Deviation: {std_dev}")
    result = math_operations.add(5, 3)
    print(f"5 + 3 = {result}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

# math_operations.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference between two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference between a and b.
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Returns the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Returns the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If the divisor is zero.
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b

# statistics.py
import math

def calculate_mean(numbers):
    """
    Returns the mean of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): The list of numbers.

    Returns:
        int or float: The mean of the numbers.
    """
    return sum(numbers) / len(numbers)

def calculate_median(numbers):
    """
    Returns the median of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): The list of numbers.

    Returns:
        int or float: The median of the numbers.
    """
    numbers.sort()
    n = len(numbers)
    if n % 2 == 0:
        return (numbers[n // 2 - 1] + numbers[n // 2]) / 2
    else:
        return numbers[n // 2]

def calculate_standard_deviation(numbers):
    """
    Returns the standard deviation of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): The list of numbers.

    Returns:
        int or float: The standard deviation of the numbers.
    """
    mean = calculate_mean(numbers)
    variance = sum((x - mean) ** 2 for x in numbers) / len(numbers)
    return math.sqrt(variance)

# main.py
import math_operations
import statistics

def main():
    """
    The main function.

    This function calculates the mean, median, and standard deviation of a list of numbers,
    and then prints the result of an addition operation.
    """
    numbers = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]
    mean = statistics.calculate_mean(numbers)
    median = statistics.calculate_median(numbers)
    std_dev = statistics.calculate_standard_deviation(numbers)
    print(f"Mean: {mean}, Median: {median}, Standard Deviation: {std_dev}")
    result = math_operations.add(5, 3)
    print(f"5 + 3 = {result}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

import math

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return math.pi * radius ** 2

def calculate_circumference(radius):
    """
    Calculate the circumference of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The circumference of the circle.
    """
    return 2 * math.pi * radius

class Circle:
    """
    A class representing a circle.

    Attributes:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.
    """

    def __init__(self, radius):
        """
        Initialize a Circle object.

        Args:
            radius (float): The radius of the circle.
        """
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def circumference(self):
        """
        Calculate the circumference of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The circumference of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_circumference(self.radius)

import math

def calculate_distance(point1, point2):
    return math.sqrt((point2[0] - point1[0])**2 + (point2[1] - point1[1])**2)

def calculate_angle(point1, point2, point3):
    a = calculate_distance(point2, point1)
    b = calculate_distance(point2, point3)
    c = calculate_distance(point1, point3)
    return math.acos((a**2 + b**2 - c**2) / (2 * a * b))

class Geometry:
    def __init__(self):
        pass

    def calculate_perimeter(self, points):
        perimeter = 0
        for i in range(len(points)):
            perimeter += calculate_distance(points[i], points[(i+1)%len(points)])
        return perimeter

    def calculate_area(self, points):
        area = 0
        for i in range(len(points)):
            area += points[i][0] * points[(i+1)%len(points)][1]
            area -= points[(i+1)%len(points)][0] * points[i][1]
        return abs(area) / 2

<BEGIN_RESPONSE>
import math

def calculate_distance(point1, point2):
    """
    Calculate the Euclidean distance between two points.

    Args:
        point1 (tuple): The coordinates of the first point.
        point2 (tuple): The coordinates of the second point.

    Returns:
        float: The distance between the two points.
    """
    return math.sqrt((point2[0] - point1[0])**2 + (point2[1] - point1[1])**2)

def calculate_angle(point1, point2, point3):
    """
    Calculate the angle between three points.

    Args:
        point1 (tuple): The coordinates of the first point.
        point2 (tuple): The coordinates of the second point.
        point3 (tuple): The coordinates of the third point.

    Returns:
        float: The angle between the three points in radians.
    """
    a = calculate_distance(point2, point1)
    b = calculate_distance(point2, point3)
    c = calculate_distance(point1, point3)
    return math.acos((a**2 + b**2 - c**2) / (2 * a * b))

class Geometry:
    """
    A class for geometric calculations.
    """

    def __init__(self):
        """
        Initialize the Geometry class.
        """
        pass

    def calculate_perimeter(self, points):
        """
        Calculate the perimeter of a polygon.

        Args:
            points (list): A list of tuples representing the coordinates of the points.

        Returns:
            float: The perimeter of the polygon.
        """
        perimeter = 0
        for i in range(len(points)):
            perimeter += calculate_distance(points[i], points[(i+1)%len(points)])
        return perimeter

    def calculate_area(self, points):
        """
        Calculate the area of a polygon using the Shoelace formula.

        Args:
            points (list): A list of tuples representing the coordinates of the points.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the polygon.
        """
        area = 0
        for i in range(len(points)):
            area += points[i][0] * points[(i+1)%len(points)][1]
            area -= points[(i+1)%len(points)][0] * points[i][1]
        return abs(area) / 2
<END_RESPONSE>

    return 2 * math.pi * radius

    return 2 * radius

class Circle:
    def __init__(self, radius):
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def circumference(self):
        return calculate_circumference(self.radius)

    def diameter(self):
        return calculate_diameter(self.radius)

import math

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return math.pi * radius ** 2

def calculate_circumference(radius):
    """
    Calculate the circumference of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The circumference of the circle.
    """
    return 2 * math.pi * radius

def calculate_diameter(radius):
    """
    Calculate the diameter of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The diameter of the circle.
    """
    return 2 * radius

class Circle:
    """
    A class representing a circle.

    Attributes:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.
    """

    def __init__(self, radius):
        """
        Initialize a Circle object.

        Args:
            radius (float): The radius of the circle.
        """
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def circumference(self):
        """
        Calculate the circumference of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The circumference of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_circumference(self.radius)

    def diameter(self):
        """
        Calculate the diameter of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The diameter of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_diameter(self.radius)

# math_operations.py
def add(x, y):
    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number to add.
        y (int or float): The second number to add.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> add(3, 5)
        8
    """
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    """
    Subtracts one number from another.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The number to subtract from.
        y (int or float): The number to subtract.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference between x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(10, 4)
        6
    """
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    """
    Multiplies two numbers together.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number to multiply.
        y (int or float): The second number to multiply.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(4, 5)
        20
    """
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    """
    Divides one number by another.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The number to divide.
        y (int or float): The number to divide by.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of x and y.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If y is zero.

    Examples:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5
    """
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return x / y

Here's why:

1. **Lack of context**: Automatically generated docstrings might not fully capture the nuances of the code, leading to incomplete or inaccurate documentation.
2. **Over-documentation**: Generating docstrings for every single function and module can result in information overload, making it harder for developers to focus on the most critical aspects of the code.

Instead of generating docstrings for all modules and functions, I recommend a more targeted approach:

1. **Focus on critical components**: Identify the most complex or business-critical parts of the codebase and prioritize writing high-quality docstrings for those areas.
2. **Use automated tools judiciously**: Utilize automated documentation tools to generate basic docstrings, but review and refine them to ensure accuracy and relevance.

def calculate_area(length, width):
    """
    Calculate the area of a rectangle.

    Args:
        length (float): The length of the rectangle.
        width (float): The width of the rectangle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the rectangle.

    Example:
        >>> calculate_area(5, 3)
        15
    """
    return length * width

def calculate_perimeter(length, width):
    """
    Calculate the perimeter of a rectangle.

    Args:
        length (float): The length of the rectangle.
        width (float): The width of the rectangle.

    Returns:
        float: The perimeter of the rectangle.

    Example:
        >>> calculate_perimeter(5, 3)
        16
    """
    return 2 * (length + width)

class Rectangle:
    """
    A class representing a rectangle.

    Attributes:
        length (float): The length of the rectangle.
        width (float): The width of the rectangle.
    """

    def __init__(self, length, width):
        """
        Initialize a Rectangle object.

        Args:
            length (float): The length of the rectangle.
            width (float): The width of the rectangle.
        """
        self.length = length
        self.width = width

    def area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the rectangle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the rectangle.

        Example:
            >>> rect = Rectangle(5, 3)
            >>> rect.area()
            15
        """
        return calculate_area(self.length, self.width)

    def perimeter(self):
        """
        Calculate the perimeter of the rectangle.

        Returns:
            float: The perimeter of the rectangle.

        Example:
            >>> rect = Rectangle(5, 3)
            >>> rect.perimeter()
            16
        """
        return calculate_perimeter(self.length, self.width)

    """

    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.
    """
    return a - b

class Calculator:
    """
    A class used to perform mathematical operations.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The name of the calculator.
    """

    def __init__(self, name):
        """
        Initializes the Calculator object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the calculator.
        """
        self.name = name

    def multiply(self, a, b):
        """
        Returns the product of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int or float): The first number.
            b (int or float): The second number.

        Returns:
            int or float: The product of a and b.
        """
        return a * b

    def divide(self, a, b):
        """
        Returns the quotient of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int or float): The dividend.
            b (int or float): The divisor.

        Returns:
            int or float: The quotient of a and b.

        Raises:
            ValueError: If the divisor is zero.
        """
        if b == 0:
            raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
        return a / b

import math

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return math.pi * radius ** 2

def calculate_circumference(radius):
    """
    Calculate the circumference of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The circumference of the circle.
    """
    return 2 * math.pi * radius

class Circle:
    """
    A class representing a circle.

    Attributes:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.
    """

    def __init__(self, radius):
        """
        Initialize a Circle object.

        Args:
            radius (float): The radius of the circle.
        """
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def circumference(self):
        """
        Calculate the circumference of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The circumference of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_circumference(self.radius)

from typing import List, Dict

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Return a personalized greeting.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A personalized greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def calculate_total(prices: List[float]) -> float:
    """
    Calculate the total cost of a list of prices.

    Args:
        prices (List[float]): A list of prices.

    Returns:
        float: The total cost.
    """
    return sum(prices)

def find_user(users: Dict[int, str], user_id: int) -> str:
    """
    Find a user by their ID.

    Args:
        users (Dict[int, str]): A dictionary of users.
        user_id (int): The ID of the user to find.

    Returns:
        str: The name of the user if found, otherwise None.
    """
    return users.get(user_id)

class Calculator:
    def __init__(self, num1: float, num2: float):
        """
        Initialize a calculator with two numbers.

        Args:
            num1 (float): The first number.
            num2 (float): The second number.
        """
        self.num1 = num1
        self.num2 = num2

    def add(self) -> float:
        """
        Add the two numbers.

        Returns:
            float: The sum of the two numbers.
        """
        return self.num1 + self.num2

    def subtract(self) -> float:
        """
        Subtract the two numbers.

        Returns:
            float: The difference of the two numbers.
        """
        return self.num1 - self.num2

import math

def calculate_distance(x1, y1, x2, y2):
    """
    Calculate the Euclidean distance between two points.

    Args:
        x1 (float): The x-coordinate of the first point.
        y1 (float): The y-coordinate of the first point.
        x2 (float): The x-coordinate of the second point.
        y2 (float): The y-coordinate of the second point.

    Returns:
        float: The distance between the two points.
    """
    return math.sqrt((x2 - x1)**2 + (y2 - y1)**2)

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return math.pi * radius**2

class Circle:
    """
    A class representing a circle.

    Attributes:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.
    """

    def __init__(self, radius):
        """
        Initialize a Circle object.

        Args:
            radius (float): The radius of the circle.
        """
        self.radius = radius

    def calculate_circumference(self):
        """
        Calculate the circumference of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The circumference of the circle.
        """
        return 2 * math.pi * self.radius

    def calculate_area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the circle.
        """
        return math.pi * self.radius**2
<END_RESPONSE>

    return a - b

<BEGIN_RESPONSE>
While generating Python docstrings for the given modules and functions is a good practice, it's essential to consider the potential drawbacks of relying solely on automated documentation tools.

```python
# my_module.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.

    Notes:
        This function does not handle non-numeric inputs.
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The difference of a and b.

    Notes:
        This function does not handle non-numeric inputs.
    """
    return a - b
```

However, over-reliance on automated documentation can lead to:

1.  **Inaccurate or incomplete documentation**: Automated tools may not always capture the nuances of the code or its intended behavior.
2.  **Lack of human insight**: Documentation generated solely by machines may lack the context and expertise that a human developer can provide.
3.  **Dependence on tooling**: Relying too heavily on automated documentation tools can make it difficult to maintain or update documentation when those tools are no longer available or supported.

To mitigate these risks, it's crucial to review and refine automated documentation to ensure it accurately reflects the code's behavior and intent. Additionally, developers should strive to write clear, readable code that is self-documenting, reducing the need for extensive external documentation.
<END_RESPONSE>

    return f"Hello, {name}!"

    return a + b

class Calculator:
    def __init__(self, num1: int, num2: int):
        self.num1 = num1
        self.num2 = num2

    def multiply(self) -> int:
        return self.num1 * self.num2

# my_module.py
"""
This module contains functions and classes for basic mathematical operations and greetings.

Functions:
    greet(name: str) -> str: Returns a personalized greeting message.
    add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int: Adds two numbers and returns the result.

Classes:
    Calculator: A class for performing multiplication of two numbers.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Adds two numbers and returns the result.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Calculator:
    """
    A class for performing multiplication of two numbers.

    Attributes:
        num1 (int): The first number.
        num2 (int): The second number.
    """

    def __init__(self, num1: int, num2: int):
        """
        Initializes the Calculator object.

        Args:
            num1 (int): The first number.
            num2 (int): The second number.
        """
        self.num1 = num1
        self.num2 = num2

    def multiply(self) -> int:
        """
        Multiplies the two numbers and returns the result.

        Returns:
            int: The product of num1 and num2.
        """
        return self.num1 * self.num2
<END_RESPONSE>

# math_operations.py
def add(a, b):
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b

# statistics.py
import math_operations

def calculate_mean(numbers):
    return sum(numbers) / len(numbers)

def calculate_median(numbers):
    numbers.sort()
    n = len(numbers)
    if n % 2 == 0:
        median = (numbers[n//2 - 1] + numbers[n//2]) / 2
    else:
        median = numbers[n//2]
    return median

def calculate_standard_deviation(numbers):
    mean = calculate_mean(numbers)
    variance = sum((x - mean) ** 2 for x in numbers) / len(numbers)
    return math_operations.sqrt(variance)

# math_operations.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Returns the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Returns the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If b is zero.
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b

# statistics.py
import math_operations

def calculate_mean(numbers):
    """
    Returns the mean of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        int or float: The mean of the numbers.
    """
    return sum(numbers) / len(numbers)

def calculate_median(numbers):
    """
    Returns the median of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        int or float: The median of the numbers.
    """
    numbers.sort()
    n = len(numbers)
    if n % 2 == 0:
        median = (numbers[n//2 - 1] + numbers[n//2]) / 2
    else:
        median = numbers[n//2]
    return median

def calculate_standard_deviation(numbers):
    """
    Returns the standard deviation of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        int or float: The standard deviation of the numbers.
    """
    mean = calculate_mean(numbers)
    variance = sum((x - mean) ** 2 for x in numbers) / len(numbers)
    return math_operations.sqrt(variance)

        int: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add_numbers(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

class Calculator:
    def __init__(self):
        """
        Initialize a calculator object.
        """
        pass

    def multiply(self, a: int, b: int) -> int:
        """
        Return the product of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int): The first number.
            b (int): The second number.

        Returns:
            int: The product of a and b.

        Examples:
            >>> calc = Calculator()
            >>> calc.multiply(4, 5)
            20
        """
        return a * b

# Module: math_utils.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number to add.
        b (int or float): The second number to add.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Subtracts one number from another.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The number to subtract from.
        b (int or float): The number to subtract.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference between a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Multiplies two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number to multiply.
        b (int or float): The second number to multiply.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(4, 5)
        20
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Divides one number by another.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The number to divide.
        b (int or float): The number to divide by.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If b is zero.

    Examples:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5.0
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return a / b

# Module: string_utils.py
def greet(name):
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name to use in the greeting.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.

    Examples:
        >>> greet("Alice")
        'Hello, Alice!'
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def farewell(name):
    """
    Returns a personalized farewell message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name to use in the farewell.

    Returns:
        str: A farewell message.

    Examples:
        >>> farewell("Bob")
        'Goodbye, Bob!'
    """
    return f"Goodbye, {name}!"

class Rectangle:
    def __init__(self, length: float, width: float):
        """Initializes a Rectangle object."""
        self.length = length
        self.width = width

    def get_area(self) -> float:
        """Returns the area of the rectangle."""

    Returns:
        float: The area of the rectangle.
    """
    return length * width

class Rectangle:
    def __init__(self, length: float, width: float):
        """
        Initializes a Rectangle object.

        Args:
            length (float): The length of the rectangle.
            width (float): The width of the rectangle.
        """
        self.length = length
        self.width = width

    def get_area(self) -> float:
        """
        Returns the area of the rectangle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the rectangle.
        """
        return self.length * self.width

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    A class representing a person.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The person's name.
        age (int): The person's age.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The person's name.
            age (int): The person's age.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I'm {self.age} years old."

# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Return a personalized greeting.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A personalized greeting message.

    Examples:
        >>> greet("John")
        "Hello, John!"
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Return the sum of two integers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first integer.
        b (int): The second integer.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initialize a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.

        Attributes:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Return a greeting from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message from the person.

        Examples:
            >>> person = Person("Jane", 30)
            >>> person.say_hello()
            "Hello, my name is Jane and I'm 30 years old."
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I'm {self.age} years old."

Functions:

Classes:

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.

    return f"Hello, {name}!"

    Returns the sum of two integers.

        b (int): The second integer.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

    return math.pi * radius ** 2

    return 2 * math.pi * radius

class Circle:
    def __init__(self, radius):
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def circumference(self):
        return calculate_circumference(self.radius)

import math

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return math.pi * radius ** 2

def calculate_circumference(radius):
    """
    Calculate the circumference of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The circumference of the circle.
    """
    return 2 * math.pi * radius

class Circle:
    """
    A class representing a circle.

    Attributes:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.
    """

    def __init__(self, radius):
        """
        Initialize a Circle object.

        Args:
            radius (float): The radius of the circle.
        """
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def circumference(self):
        """
        Calculate the circumference of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The circumference of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_circumference(self.radius)
<END_RESPONSE>

# math_operations.py
def add(a, b):
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b

# string_operations.py
def concatenate(str1, str2):
    return str1 + str2

def repeat_string(str, times):
    return str * times

def string_length(str):
    return len(str)

# math_operations.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(5, 3)
        8
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(10, 4)
        6
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Returns the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(7, 2)
        14
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Returns the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If b is zero.

    Examples:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b

# string_operations.py
def concatenate(str1, str2):
    """
    Returns the concatenation of two strings.

    Args:
        str1 (str): The first string.
        str2 (str): The second string.

    Returns:
        str: The concatenation of str1 and str2.

    Examples:
        >>> concatenate("Hello, ", "world!")
        'Hello, world!'
    """
    return str1 + str2

def repeat_string(str, times):
    """
    Returns the string repeated a specified number of times.

    Args:
        str (str): The string to repeat.
        times (int): The number of times to repeat the string.

    Returns:
        str: The repeated string.

    Examples:
        >>> repeat_string("Hello", 3)
        'HelloHelloHello'
    """
    return str * times

def string_length(str):
    """
    Returns the length of a string.

    Args:
        str (str): The string.

    Returns:
        int: The length of the string.

    Examples:
        >>> string_length("Hello")
        5
    """
    return len(str)

# my_module.py
"""
This module contains various utility functions and classes.

Functions:
    greet(name: str) -> str: Returns a personalized greeting message.
    add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int: Returns the sum of two numbers.

Classes:
    Person: Represents a person with a name and age.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The person's name.
        age (int): The person's age.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The person's name.
            age (int): The person's age.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."

# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> None:
    """
    Prints a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        None
    """
    print(f"Hello, {name}!")

def add(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two integers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first integer.
        b (int): The second integer.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The person's name.
        age (int): The person's age.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The person's name.
            age (int): The person's age.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> None:
        """
        Prints a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            None
        """
        print(f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old.")

# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> None:
    """Print a personalized greeting."""
    print(f"Hello, {name}!")

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """Return the sum of two numbers."""
    return a + b

class Person:
    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int) -> None:
        """Initialize a Person object."""
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> None:
        """Print a greeting from the person."""
        print(f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I'm {self.age} years old.")

# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> None:
    """
    Print a personalized greeting.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        None
    """
    print(f"Hello, {name}!")

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Return the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int) -> None:
        """
        Initialize a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The person's name.
            age (int): The person's age.

        Returns:
            None
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> None:
        """
        Print a greeting from the person.

        Returns:
            None
        """
        print(f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I'm {self.age} years old.")
<END_RESPONSE>

# This is a simple calculator module
def add(x, y):
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y

# This is a simple calculator module
def add(x, y):
    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number to add.
        y (int or float): The second number to add.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    """
    Subtracts one number from another.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The number to subtract from.
        y (int or float): The number to subtract.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    """
    Multiplies two numbers together.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number to multiply.
        y (int or float): The second number to multiply.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(4, 5)
        20
    """
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    """
    Divides one number by another.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The number to divide.
        y (int or float): The number to divide by.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of x and y.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If y is zero.

    Examples:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5.0
    """
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y

# This is a simple calculator module
def add(x, y):
    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number to add.
        y (int or float): The second number to add.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of x and y.
    """
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    """
    Subtracts one number from another.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The number to subtract from.
        y (int or float): The number to subtract.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of x and y.
    """
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    """
    Multiplies two numbers together.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number to multiply.
        y (int or float): The second number to multiply.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of x and y.
    """
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    """
    Divides one number by another.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The number to divide.
        y (int or float): The number to divide by.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of x and y.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If y is zero.
    """
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y

    Returns:

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The person's name.
        age (int): The person's age.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int) -> None:
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

            name (str): The person's name.
            age (int): The person's age.

        self.name = name
        self.age = age

# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Return a personalized greeting.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A personalized greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def sum_numbers(numbers: list[int]) -> int:
    """
    Return the sum of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list[int]): A list of numbers to sum.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of the numbers in the list.
    """
    return sum(numbers)

class Person:
    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initialize a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Return a greeting from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message from the person.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I'm {self.age} years old."

def greet(name: str) -> None:
    """
    Prints a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        None
    """
    print(f"Hello, {name}!")

def add(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two integers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first integer.
        b (int): The second integer.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The person's name.
        age (int): The person's age.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int) -> None:
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The person's name.
            age (int): The person's age.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> None:
        """
        Prints a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            None
        """
        print(f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old.")

# Module: math_operations
"""
This module provides basic mathematical operations.

Functions:
    add(a, b): Returns the sum of a and b.
    subtract(a, b): Returns the difference of a and b.
    multiply(a, b): Returns the product of a and b.
    divide(a, b): Returns the quotient of a and b.
"""

def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of a and b.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of a and b.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Returns the product of a and b.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Returns the quotient of a and b.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If b is zero.
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b

# Module: string_operations
"""
This module provides basic string operations.

Functions:
    concatenate(str1, str2): Returns the concatenation of str1 and str2.
    uppercase(str): Returns the uppercase version of str.
    lowercase(str): Returns the lowercase version of str.
"""

def concatenate(str1, str2):
    """
    Returns the concatenation of str1 and str2.

    Args:
        str1 (str): The first string.
        str2 (str): The second string.

    Returns:
        str: The concatenation of str1 and str2.
    """
    return str1 + str2

def uppercase(str):
    """
    Returns the uppercase version of str.

    Args:
        str (str): The input string.

    Returns:
        str: The uppercase version of str.
    """
    return str.upper()

def lowercase(str):
    """
    Returns the lowercase version of str.

    Args:
        str (str): The input string.

    Returns:
        str: The lowercase version of str.
    """
    return str.lower()

# my_module.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(3, 5)
        8
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(10, 4)
        6
    """
    return a - b

class Calculator:
    """
    A simple calculator class.

    Attributes:
        None

    Methods:
        multiply(a, b): Returns the product of two numbers.
        divide(a, b): Returns the quotient of two numbers.
    """

    def __init__(self):
        """
        Initializes the Calculator object.

        Args:
            None

        Returns:
            None
        """
        pass

    def multiply(self, a, b):
        """
        Returns the product of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int or float): The first number.
            b (int or float): The second number.

        Returns:
            int or float: The product of a and b.

        Examples:
            >>> calculator = Calculator()
            >>> calculator.multiply(4, 5)
            20
        """
        return a * b

    def divide(self, a, b):
        """
        Returns the quotient of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int or float): The dividend.
            b (int or float): The divisor.

        Returns:
            int or float: The quotient of a and b.

        Raises:
            ValueError: If the divisor is zero.

        Examples:
            >>> calculator = Calculator()
            >>> calculator.divide(10, 2)
            5.0
        """
        if b == 0:
            raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
        return a / b

Functions:
    greet(name: str) -> str: Returns a personalized greeting message.
    sum_numbers(numbers: list[int]) -> int: Returns the sum of a list of numbers.

Classes:
    Person: Represents a person with a name and age.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def sum_numbers(numbers: list[int]) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list[int]): A list of numbers to sum.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of the numbers.
    """
    return sum(numbers)

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The name of the person.
        age (int): The age of the person.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."

# my_module.py
"""
This module contains various utility functions and classes.

Functions:
    greet(name: str) -> str: Returns a personalized greeting message.
    add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int: Returns the sum of two numbers.

Classes:
    Person: Represents a person with a name and age.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The name of the person.
        age (int): The age of the person.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."

# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> None:
    print(f"Hello, {name}!")

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    return a + b

class Person:
    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> None:
        print(f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old.")
<END_TEXT>

<BEGIN_RESPONSE>
# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> None:
    """
    Prints a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        None
    """
    print(f"Hello, {name}!")

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number to add.
        b (int): The second number to add.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    A class representing a person.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The person's name.
        age (int): The person's age.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The person's name.
            age (int): The person's age.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> None:
        """
        Prints a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            None
        """
        print(f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old.")
<END_RESPONSE>

"""
This module contains various utility functions and classes.

Functions:
    greet(name: str) -> str: Returns a personalized greeting message.
    add(a: int, b: int) -> int: Returns the sum of two integers.

Classes:
    Person: Represents a person with a name and age.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two integers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first integer.
        b (int): The second integer.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The name of the person.
        age (int): The age of the person.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."

# my_module.py
"""
This module contains various utility functions and classes.

Functions:
    greet(name: str) -> str: Returns a personalized greeting message.
    add(a: int, b: int) -> int: Returns the sum of two integers.

Classes:
    Person: Represents a person with a name and age.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two integers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first integer.
        b (int): The second integer.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The name of the person.
        age (int): The age of the person.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."
<END_RESPONSE>

# my_module.py
"""
This module contains functions and classes for various purposes.

Functions:
    greet(name: str) -> str: Returns a personalized greeting message.
    sum_numbers(numbers: list[int]) -> int: Returns the sum of a list of numbers.

Classes:
    Person: Represents a person with a name and age.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def sum_numbers(numbers: list[int]) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list[int]): A list of numbers to sum.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of the numbers.
    """
    return sum(numbers)

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The name of the person.
        age (int): The age of the person.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."

# This is a simple calculator module
def add(x, y):
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y
