# This is a simple calculator module
def add(x, y):
    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number to add.
        y (int or float): The second number to add.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of x and y.
    """
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    """
    Subtracts one number from another.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The number to subtract from.
        y (int or float): The number to subtract.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of x and y.
    """
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    """
    Multiplies two numbers together.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number to multiply.
        y (int or float): The second number to multiply.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of x and y.
    """
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    """
    Divides one number by another.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The number to divide.
        y (int or float): The number to divide by.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of x and y.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If y is zero.
    """
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y
<END_RESPONSE>

    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number to add.
        b (int): The second number to add.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

"""
Simple Calculator Module
========================
This module provides basic mathematical operations.

Functions
---------
"""

def add(x, y):
    """
    Add two numbers together.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of x and y.
    """
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    """
    Subtract the second number from the first.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference between x and y.
    """
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    """
    Multiply two numbers together.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of x and y.
    """
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    """
    Divide the first number by the second.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The dividend.
        y (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of x and y.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If y is zero.
    """
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y

class Calculator:
    """
    A simple calculator class.
    """

    def __init__(self):
        """
        Initializes the calculator with a result of 0.
        """
        self.result = 0

    def add(self, a, b):
        """
        Adds two numbers together and stores the result.

        Args:
            a (int): The first number to add.
            b (int): The second number to add.

        Returns:
            int: The sum of a and b.
        """
        self.result = a + b
        return self.result

    def subtract(self, a, b):
        """
        Subtracts one number from another and stores the result.

        Args:
            a (int): The number to subtract from.
            b (int): The number to subtract.

        Returns:
            int: The difference of a and b.
        """
        self.result = a - b
        return self.result

# math_operations.py
"""
Module for performing basic mathematical operations.
"""

def add(a, b):
    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Subtracts one number from another.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Multiplies two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Divides one number by another.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If the divisor is zero.
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b

# A simple math module

def add(x, y):
    """
    Return the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    """
    Return the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    """
    Return the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(4, 5)
        20
    """
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    """
    Return the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The dividend.
        y (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of x and y.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If y is zero.

    Examples:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5.0
    """
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y

# my_module.py
"""
Module to provide basic functionality.

Classes:
    MyClass: A class to store and manipulate a value.

Functions:
    greet: Return a personalized greeting.
    sum_numbers: Return the sum of a list of numbers.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Return a personalized greeting.

    Args:
        name (str): The name to use in the greeting.

    Returns:
        str: A personalized greeting.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def sum_numbers(numbers: list[int]) -> int:
    """
    Return the sum of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list[int]): A list of numbers to sum.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of the numbers.
    """
    return sum(numbers)

class MyClass:
    """
    A class to store and manipulate a value.

    Attributes:
        value (int): The value stored in the class.
    """

    def __init__(self, value: int):
        """
        Initialize the class with a value.

        Args:
            value (int): The value to store in the class.
        """
        self.value = value

    def double_value(self) -> int:
        """
        Return the double of the class value.

        Returns:
            int: The double of the class value.
        """
        return self.value * 2

# math_utils.py
def add_numbers(a, b):
    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number to add.
        b (int or float): The second number to add.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add_numbers(5, 3)
        8
    """
    return a + b

def multiply_numbers(a, b):
    """
    Multiplies two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number to multiply.
        b (int or float): The second number to multiply.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply_numbers(5, 3)
        15
    """
    return a * b

# string_utils.py
def capitalize_string(s):
    """
    Capitalizes a given string.

    Args:
        s (str): The string to capitalize.

    Returns:
        str: The capitalized string.

    Examples:
        >>> capitalize_string("hello")
        'HELLO'
    """
    return s.upper()

def lower_case_string(s):
    """
    Converts a given string to lower case.

    Args:
        s (str): The string to convert.

    Returns:
        str: The lower case string.

    Examples:
        >>> lower_case_string("HELLO")
        'hello'
    """
    return s.lower()

# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def sum_numbers(numbers: list[int]) -> int:
    """
    Calculates the sum of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list[int]): A list of integers to sum.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of the numbers.
    """
    return sum(numbers)

# The concept of docstrings in Python was first introduced in Python 2.1, released in 2001.
# The idea was to provide a standardized way of documenting modules, functions, and classes.
# Since then, docstrings have become an essential part of Python coding standards.

# Module: math_operations
def add(x, y):
    """
    Return the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> add(3, 5)
        8
        >>> add(3.5, 2.7)
        6.2
    """
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    """
    Return the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(8, 3)
        5
        >>> subtract(3.5, 2.7)
        0.8
    """
    return x - y

# Module: string_operations
def concatenate(str1, str2):
    """
    Return the concatenation of two strings.

    Args:
        str1 (str): The first string.
        str2 (str): The second string.

    Returns:
        str: The concatenation of str1 and str2.

    Examples:
        >>> concatenate("Hello, ", "world!")
        'Hello, world!'
        >>> concatenate(" Foo ", "Bar ")
        ' Foo Bar '
    """
    return str1 + str2

def split_string(str):
    """
    Return a list of words in a string.

    Args:
        str (str): The input string.

    Returns:
        list: A list of words in the input string.

    Examples:
        >>> split_string("Hello world!")
        ['Hello', 'world!']
        >>> split_string(" Foo Bar Baz ")
        ['Foo', 'Bar', 'Baz']
    """
    return str.split()

def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The difference of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return a - b

However, I must highlight that generating docstrings for given modules and functions can be a flawed approach. Here's why:

1.  **Lack of Context**: Without understanding the purpose and behavior of the code, generated docstrings may not accurately convey the intended functionality.
2.  **Insufficient Information**: Relying solely on function signatures and code structure can lead to incomplete or misleading documentation.
3.  **Overemphasis on Syntax**: Focusing on generating docstrings may distract from the importance of writing clear, readable, and well-structured code in the first place.

A better approach might be to prioritize writing high-quality, readable code and then supplementing it with docstrings that provide additional context and explanation. This way, the code itself serves as the primary documentation, and the docstrings enhance understanding rather than being the sole source of information.

    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number to be added.
        b (int): The second number to be added.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.

class Calculator:
    """
    A class used to represent a calculator.

    Attributes:
        brand (str): The brand of the calculator.
        model (str): The model of the calculator.
    """

    def __init__(self, brand: str, model: str):
        """
        Initializes the Calculator object.

        Args:
            brand (str): The brand of the calculator.
            model (str): The model of the calculator.
        """
        self.brand = brand
        self.model = model

    def calculate_area(self, length: int, width: int) -> int:
        """
        Calculates the area of a rectangle.

        Args:
            length (int): The length of the rectangle.
            width (int): The width of the rectangle.

        Returns:
            int: The area of the rectangle.
        """
        return length * width

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

    """
    Perform mathematical operations based on the module.

    Args:
        module (str): The module to perform the operation. Currently supports "add".

    Returns:
        None
    """
    if module == "add":
        result = add_numbers(5, 7)
        print(f"The result of addition is: {result}")

import math

def calculate_area(radius):
    return math.pi * radius ** 2

def calculate_circumference(radius):
    return 2 * math.pi * radius

class Circle:
    def __init__(self, radius):
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def circumference(self):
        return calculate_circumference(self.radius)

def main():
    circle = Circle(5)
    print(f"Area: {circle.area()}")
    print(f"Circumference: {circle.circumference()}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
<END_TEXT>
<BEGIN_RESPONSE>
import math

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.

    Examples:
        >>> calculate_area(5)
        78.53981633974483
    """
    return math.pi * radius ** 2

def calculate_circumference(radius):
    """
    Calculate the circumference of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The circumference of the circle.

    Examples:
        >>> calculate_circumference(5)
        31.41592653589793
    """
    return 2 * math.pi * radius

class Circle:
    """
    A class representing a circle.

    Attributes:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Methods:
        area: Calculate the area of the circle.
        circumference: Calculate the circumference of the circle.
    """

    def __init__(self, radius):
        """
        Initialize a Circle object.

        Args:
            radius (float): The radius of the circle.
        """
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def circumference(self):
        """
        Calculate the circumference of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The circumference of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_circumference(self.radius)

def main():
    """
    The main function of the program.

    Creates a Circle object with a radius of 5 and prints its area and circumference.
    """
    circle = Circle(5)
    print(f"Area: {circle.area()}")
    print(f"Circumference: {circle.circumference()}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

# math_utils.py
def add_numbers(a, b):
    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def subtract_numbers(a, b):
    """
    Subtracts the second number from the first.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.
    """
    return a - b

# string_utils.py
def concatenate_strings(str1, str2):
    """
    Concatenates two strings together.

    Args:
        str1 (str): The first string.
        str2 (str): The second string.

    Returns:
        str: The concatenated string.
    """
    return str1 + str2

def reverse_string(s):
    """
    Reverses a given string.

    Args:
        s (str): The string to be reversed.

    Returns:
        str: The reversed string.
    """
    return s[::-1]

# Module: math_operations
"""
This module contains basic mathematical operations.
"""

def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Returns the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Returns the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If the divisor is zero.
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b

# Module: string_operations
"""
This module contains string operations.
"""

def greet(name):
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def farewell(name):
    """
    Returns a personalized farewell message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person.

    Returns:
        str: A farewell message.
    """
    return f"Goodbye, {name}!"

import math

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return math.pi * radius ** 2

def calculate_circumference(radius):
    """
    Calculate the circumference of a circle given its radius.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The circumference of the circle.
    """
    return 2 * math.pi * radius

class Circle:
    """
    A class representing a circle.

    Attributes:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.
    """

    def __init__(self, radius):
        """
        Initialize a Circle object.

        Args:
            radius (float): The radius of the circle.
        """
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def circumference(self):
        """
        Calculate the circumference of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The circumference of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_circumference(self.radius)

module my_math
"""
This module provides basic mathematical operations.
"""

def add(a, b):
    """
    Add two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(1, 2)
        3
        >>> add(1.5, 2.5)
        4.0
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Subtract two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(3, 2)
        1
        >>> subtract(3.5, 2.5)
        1.0
    """
    return a - b

class Calculator:
    """
    A basic calculator class.
    """

    def __init__(self):
        """
        Initialize a calculator.

        Returns:
            Calculator: A new calculator instance.
        """
        pass

    def multiply(self, a, b):
        """
        Multiply two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int or float): The first number.
            b (int or float): The second number.

        Returns:
            int or float: The product of a and b.

        Examples:
            >>> calc = Calculator()
            >>> calc.multiply(2, 3)
            6
            >>> calc.multiply(2.5, 3.5)
            8.75
        """
        return a * b

    def divide(self, a, b):
        """
        Divide two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int or float): The dividend.
            b (int or float): The divisor.

        Returns:
            int or float: The quotient of a and b.

        Raises:
            ValueError: If the divisor is zero.

        Examples:
            >>> calc = Calculator()
            >>> calc.divide(6, 2)
            3
            >>> calc.divide(6.0, 2.0)
            3.0
            >>> calc.divide(6, 0)
            ValueError: Cannot divide by zero
        """
        if b == 0:
            raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
        return a / b

# math_operations.py
"""
Module for basic mathematical operations.

This module provides functions for addition, subtraction, multiplication, and division.
"""

def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Returns the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Returns the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If the divisor is zero.
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b


# string_operations.py
"""
Module for basic string operations.

This module provides functions for concatenating strings, converting strings to uppercase, and converting strings to lowercase.
"""

def concatenate(str1, str2):
    """
    Returns the concatenation of two strings.

    Args:
        str1 (str): The first string.
        str2 (str): The second string.

    Returns:
        str: The concatenation of str1 and str2.
    """
    return str1 + str2

def uppercase_string(s):
    """
    Returns the uppercase version of a string.

    Args:
        s (str): The input string.

    Returns:
        str: The uppercase version of s.
    """
    return s.upper()

def lowercase_string(s):
    """
    Returns the lowercase version of a string.

    Args:
        s (str): The input string.

    Returns:
        str: The lowercase version of s.
    """
    return s.lower()
<END_RESPONSE>
<BEGIN_TEXT>
import math
def calculate_distance(x1, y1, x2, y2):
    return math.sqrt((x2 - x1)**2 + (y2 - y1)**2)

def calculate_area(radius):
    return math.pi * radius**2

class Circle:
    def __init__(self, radius):
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def circumference(self):
        return 2 * math.pi * self.radius
<END_TEXT>

<BEGIN_RESPONSE>
While generating Python docstrings for the given modules and functions may seem like a straightforward task, it's essential to consider the potential flaws and limitations of this approach.

One major concern is the accuracy and completeness of the generated docstrings. If the docstrings are not thoroughly reviewed and tested, they may contain errors or omit critical information, leading to confusion and misinterpretation by users.

Moreover, relying solely on automated docstring generation may overlook the importance of human judgment and expertise in documenting complex code. Experienced developers and technical writers bring valuable insights and context to the documentation process, which may be lost when relying solely on automated tools.

Here is an example of how the code could be modified to include docstrings, highlighting the potential limitations of automated docstring generation:

```python
import math

def calculate_distance(x1, y1, x2, y2):
    """
    Calculate the Euclidean distance between two points.

    Args:
        x1 (float): The x-coordinate of the first point.
        y1 (float): The y-coordinate of the first point.
        x2 (float): The x-coordinate of the second point.
        y2 (float): The y-coordinate of the second point.

    Returns:
        float: The distance between the two points.

    Note:
        This function uses the math.sqrt function, which may not be suitable for all use cases.
    """
    return math.sqrt((x2 - x1)**2 + (y2 - y1)**2)

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.

    Note:
        This function uses the math.pi constant, which may not be precise enough for certain applications.
    """
    return math.pi * radius**2

class Circle:
    """
    A class representing a circle.

    Attributes:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.
    """

    def __init__(self, radius):
        """
        Initialize a Circle object.

        Args:
            radius (float): The radius of the circle.
        """
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the circle.
        """
        return calculate_area(self.radius)

    def circumference(self):
        """
        Calculate the circumference of the circle.

        Returns:
            float: The circumference of the circle.
        """
        return 2 * math.pi * self.radius
```

A more comprehensive approach to documentation would involve a combination of automated tools and human review to ensure accuracy, completeness, and clarity.

        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

# Module: music_library.py
"""
A music library class that allows you to manage a collection of songs.

Attributes:
    songs (list): A list of Song objects.
"""

class MusicLibrary:
    """
    Initializes an empty music library.

    Attributes:
        songs (list): A list of Song objects.
    """
    def __init__(self):
        self.songs = []

    """
    Adds a song to the music library.

    Args:
        song (Song): The song to be added.

    Returns:
        None
    """
    def add_song(self, song):
        self.songs.append(song)

    """
    Removes a song from the music library.

    Args:
        song (Song): The song to be removed.

    Returns:
        None
    """
    def remove_song(self, song):
        self.songs.remove(song)

# Module: song.py
"""
A song class that represents a song with a title and an artist.

Attributes:
    title (str): The title of the song.
    artist (str): The artist of the song.
"""

class Song:
    """
    Initializes a song with a title and an artist.

    Args:
        title (str): The title of the song.
        artist (str): The artist of the song.

    Attributes:
        title (str): The title of the song.
        artist (str): The artist of the song.
    """
    def __init__(self, title, artist):
        self.title = title
        self.artist = artist

    """
    Plays the song.

    Returns:
        None
    """
    def play(self):
        print(f"Now playing: {self.title} by {self.artist}")

import math

def calculate_distance(x1, y1, x2, y2):
    return math.sqrt((x2 - x1)**2 + (y2 - y1)**2)

def calculate_area(radius):
    return math.pi * radius**2

class Geometry:
    def __init__(self, shape):
        self.shape = shape

    def calculate_perimeter(self):
        if self.shape == 'circle':
            return 2 * math.pi * self.radius
        elif self.shape == 'rectangle':
            return 2 * (self.length + self.width)

    def calculate_area(self):
        if self.shape == 'circle':
            return math.pi * self.radius**2
        elif self.shape == 'rectangle':
            return self.length * self.width

import math

def calculate_distance(x1, y1, x2, y2):
    """
    Calculate the distance between two points in a 2D space.

    Args:
        x1 (float): The x-coordinate of the first point.
        y1 (float): The y-coordinate of the first point.
        x2 (float): The x-coordinate of the second point.
        y2 (float): The y-coordinate of the second point.

    Returns:
        float: The distance between the two points.
    """
    return math.sqrt((x2 - x1)**2 + (y2 - y1)**2)

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return math.pi * radius**2

class Geometry:
    """
    A class used to represent a geometric shape.

    Attributes:
        shape (str): The type of shape (e.g. 'circle', 'rectangle').
    """

    def __init__(self, shape):
        """
        Initialize the Geometry object.

        Args:
            shape (str): The type of shape.
        """
        self.shape = shape

    def calculate_perimeter(self):
        """
        Calculate the perimeter of the shape.

        Returns:
            float: The perimeter of the shape.
        """
        if self.shape == 'circle':
            return 2 * math.pi * self.radius
        elif self.shape == 'rectangle':
            return 2 * (self.length + self.width)

    def calculate_area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the shape.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the shape.
        """
        if self.shape == 'circle':
            return math.pi * self.radius**2
        elif self.shape == 'rectangle':
            return self.length * self.width
<END_RESPONSE>

```
def calculate_area(base, height):
    """
    Calculate the area of a triangle.

    Args:
        base (float): The base of the triangle.
        height (float): The height of the triangle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the triangle.

    Examples:
        >>> calculate_area(3, 4)
        6.0
    """
    return 0.5 * base * height

def calculate_perimeter(base, height):
    """
    Calculate the perimeter of a triangle.

    Args:
        base (float): The base of the triangle.
        height (float): The height of the triangle.

    Returns:
        float: The perimeter of the triangle.

    Examples:
        >>> calculate_perimeter(3, 4)
        10.0
    """
    return base + height + (base**2 + height**2)**0.5
```

# Import the math module for mathematical operations
import math

# Function to calculate the distance between two points
def calculate_distance(x1, y1, x2, y2):
    """
    Calculate the distance between two points.

    Args:
        x1 (float): The x-coordinate of the first point.
        y1 (float): The y-coordinate of the first point.
        x2 (float): The x-coordinate of the second point.
        y2 (float): The y-coordinate of the second point.

    Returns:
        float: The distance between the two points.

    Example:
        >>> calculate_distance(1, 2, 4, 6)
        5.0
    """
    return math.sqrt((x2 - x1)**2 + (y2 - y1)**2)

# Function to calculate the area of a circle
def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.

    Example:
        >>> calculate_area(5)
        78.53981633974483
    """
    return math.pi * radius**2

# Class to perform basic arithmetic operations
class Calculator:
    def __init__(self):
        """
        Initialize the Calculator class.
        """
        pass

    # Method to add two numbers
    def add(self, a, b):
        """
        Add two numbers.

        Args:
            a (float): The first number.
            b (float): The second number.

        Returns:
            float: The sum of the two numbers.

        Example:
            >>> calculator = Calculator()
            >>> calculator.add(5, 3)
            8
        """
        return a + b

    # Method to subtract two numbers
    def subtract(self, a, b):
        """
        Subtract two numbers.

        Args:
            a (float): The first number.
            b (float): The second number.

        Returns:
            float: The difference between the two numbers.

        Example:
            >>> calculator = Calculator()
            >>> calculator.subtract(10, 4)
            6
        """
        return a - b

def subtract(x, y):

def multiply(x, y):
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y

# statistics.py
def mean(numbers):
    return sum(numbers) / len(numbers)

def median(numbers):
    numbers.sort()
    n = len(numbers)
    if n % 2 == 0:
        return (numbers[n//2 - 1] + numbers[n//2]) / 2
    else:
        return numbers[n//2]

# calculator.py
def add(x, y):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    """
    Returns the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(4, 5)
        20
    """
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    """
    Returns the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The dividend.
        y (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of x and y.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If y is zero.

    Examples:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5.0
    """
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y

# statistics.py
def mean(numbers):
    """
    Returns the mean of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        int or float: The mean of the numbers.

    Examples:
        >>> mean([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])
        3.0
    """
    return sum(numbers) / len(numbers)

def median(numbers):
    """
    Returns the median of a list of numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        int or float: The median of the numbers.

    Examples:
        >>> median([1, 3, 5])
        3
        >>> median([1, 2, 3, 4])
        2.5
    """
    numbers.sort()
    n = len(numbers)
    if n % 2 == 0:
        return (numbers[n//2 - 1] + numbers[n//2]) / 2
    else:
        return numbers[n//2]

# my_module.py
"""
This module contains functions and classes for various tasks.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."

    return length * width

def calculate_perimeter(length, width):
    return 2 * (length + width)

    def __init__(self, length, width):
        self.length = length

def calculate_area(length, width):
    """
    Calculate the area of a rectangle.

    Args:
        length (float): The length of the rectangle.
        width (float): The width of the rectangle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the rectangle.

    Notes:
        This function assumes that the input values are valid numbers.
    """
    return length * width

def calculate_perimeter(length, width):
    """
    Calculate the perimeter of a rectangle.

    Args:
        length (float): The length of the rectangle.
        width (float): The width of the rectangle.

    Returns:
        float: The perimeter of the rectangle.

    Notes:
        This function assumes that the input values are valid numbers.
    """
    return 2 * (length + width)

class Rectangle:
    """
    A class representing a rectangle.

    Attributes:
        length (float): The length of the rectangle.
        width (float): The width of the rectangle.
    """

    def __init__(self, length, width):
        """
        Initialize a Rectangle object.

        Args:
            length (float): The length of the rectangle.
            width (float): The width of the rectangle.

        Raises:
            ValueError: If either length or width is not a positive number.
        """
        if length <= 0 or width <= 0:
            raise ValueError("Length and width must be positive numbers")
        self.length = length
        self.width = width

    def area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the rectangle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the rectangle.
        """
        return calculate_area(self.length, self.width)

    def perimeter(self):
        """
        Calculate the perimeter of the rectangle.

        Returns:
            float: The perimeter of the rectangle.
        """
        return calculate_perimeter(self.length, self.width)

# math_operations.py
"""
This module provides basic mathematical operations.

Functions:
    add(a, b): Returns the sum of a and b.
    subtract(a, b): Returns the difference of a and b.
    multiply(a, b): Returns the product of a and b.
    divide(a, b): Returns the quotient of a and b.
"""

def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of a and b.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of a and b.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Returns the product of a and b.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Returns the quotient of a and b.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If b is zero.
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b

# statistics.py
"""
This module provides basic statistical calculations.

Functions:
    mean(numbers): Returns the mean of the given numbers.
    median(numbers): Returns the median of the given numbers.
"""

def mean(numbers):
    """
    Returns the mean of the given numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        int or float: The mean of the given numbers.
    """
    return sum(numbers) / len(numbers)

def median(numbers):
    """
    Returns the median of the given numbers.

    Args:
        numbers (list of int or float): A list of numbers.

    Returns:
        int or float: The median of the given numbers.
    """
    numbers.sort()
    n = len(numbers)
    if n % 2 == 0:
        return (numbers[n // 2 - 1] + numbers[n // 2]) / 2
    else:
        return numbers[n // 2]

import math

def calculate_distance(point1, point2):
    return math.sqrt((point2[0] - point1[0])**2 + (point2[1] - point1[1])**2)

    return math.pi * radius**2

class Geometry:
    def __init__(self, shape):
        self.shape = shape

    def calculate_perimeter(self):
        if self.shape == 'circle':
            return 2 * math.pi * self.radius
        elif self.shape == 'rectangle':

        else:

import math

def calculate_distance(point1, point2):
    """
    Calculate the Euclidean distance between two points.

    Args:
        point1 (tuple): The coordinates of the first point.
        point2 (tuple): The coordinates of the second point.

    Returns:
        float: The Euclidean distance between the two points.

    Example:
        >>> calculate_distance((1, 2), (4, 6))
        5.0
    """
    return math.sqrt((point2[0] - point1[0])**2 + (point2[1] - point1[1])**2)

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.

    Example:
        >>> calculate_area(5)
        78.53981633974483
    """
    return math.pi * radius**2

class Geometry:
    """
    A class representing geometric shapes.

    Attributes:
        shape (str): The type of shape (e.g. 'circle', 'rectangle').

    Methods:
        calculate_perimeter: Calculate the perimeter of the shape.
        calculate_area: Calculate the area of the shape.
    """

    def __init__(self, shape):
        """
        Initialize a Geometry object.

        Args:
            shape (str): The type of shape (e.g. 'circle', 'rectangle').

        Raises:
            ValueError: If the shape is not supported.
        """
        self.shape = shape

    def calculate_perimeter(self):
        """
        Calculate the perimeter of the shape.

        Returns:
            float: The perimeter of the shape.

        Raises:
            ValueError: If the shape is not supported.

        Example:
            >>> geometry = Geometry('circle')
            >>> geometry.radius = 5
            >>> geometry.calculate_perimeter()
            31.41592653589793
        """
        if self.shape == 'circle':
            return 2 * math.pi * self.radius
        elif self.shape == 'rectangle':
            return 2 * (self.length + self.width)
        else:
            raise ValueError('Unsupported shape')

    def calculate_area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the shape.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the shape.

        Raises:
            ValueError: If the shape is not supported.

        Example:
            >>> geometry = Geometry('rectangle')
            >>> geometry.length = 5
            >>> geometry.width = 3
            >>> geometry.calculate_area()
            15
        """
        if self.shape == 'circle':
            return math.pi * self.radius**2
        elif self.shape == 'rectangle':
            return self.length * self.width
        else:
            raise ValueError('Unsupported shape')

def calculate_distance(point1, point2):
    return math.sqrt((point2[0] - point1[0])**2 + (point2[1] - point1[1])**2)

def calculate_area(radius):
    return math.pi * radius**2

class Geometry:
    def __init__(self, shape):
        self.shape = shape

    def calculate_perimeter(self):
        if self.shape == 'circle':
            return 2 * math.pi * self.radius
        elif self.shape == 'rectangle':
            return 2 * (self.length + self.width)

    def calculate_area(self):
        if self.shape == 'circle':
            return math.pi * self.radius**2
        elif self.shape == 'rectangle':
            return self.length * self.width

import math

def calculate_distance(point1, point2):
    """
    Calculate the Euclidean distance between two points.

    Args:
        point1 (tuple): The coordinates of the first point.
        point2 (tuple): The coordinates of the second point.

    Returns:
        float: The distance between the two points.
    """
    return math.sqrt((point2[0] - point1[0])**2 + (point2[1] - point1[1])**2)

def calculate_area(radius):
    """
    Calculate the area of a circle.

    Args:
        radius (float): The radius of the circle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the circle.
    """
    return math.pi * radius**2

class Geometry:
    """
    A class representing geometric shapes.

    Attributes:
        shape (str): The type of shape.
    """

    def __init__(self, shape):
        """
        Initialize the Geometry object.

        Args:
            shape (str): The type of shape.
        """
        self.shape = shape

    def calculate_perimeter(self):
        """
        Calculate the perimeter of the shape.

        Returns:
            float: The perimeter of the shape.

        Raises:
            AttributeError: If the shape is not 'circle' or 'rectangle'.
        """
        if self.shape == 'circle':
            return 2 * math.pi * self.radius
        elif self.shape == 'rectangle':
            return 2 * (self.length + self.width)

    def calculate_area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the shape.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the shape.

        Raises:
            AttributeError: If the shape is not 'circle' or 'rectangle'.
        """
        if self.shape == 'circle':
            return math.pi * self.radius**2
        elif self.shape == 'rectangle':
            return self.length * self.width

# math_operations.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Adds two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Subtracts one number from another.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Multiplies two numbers together.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(4, 5)
        20
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Divides one number by another.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If the divisor is zero.

    Examples:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5.0
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
    return a / b


# string_operations.py
def concatenate(a, b):
    """
    Concatenates two strings together.

    Args:
        a (str): The first string.
        b (str): The second string.

    Returns:
        str: The concatenation of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> concatenate("Hello, ", "world!")
        'Hello, world!'
    """
    return a + b

def repeat(a, n):
    """
    Repeats a string n times.

    Args:
        a (str): The string to repeat.
        n (int): The number of times to repeat the string.

    Returns:
        str: The repeated string.

    Examples:
        >>> repeat("Hello", 3)
        'HelloHelloHello'
    """
    return a * n

def uppercase(a):
    """
    Converts a string to uppercase.

    Args:
        a (str): The string to convert.

    Returns:
        str: The uppercase version of a.

    Examples:
        >>> uppercase("hello")
        'HELLO'
    """
    return a.upper()

# This is a Python module that provides functions for calculating mathematical operations.
# The module was created in 2022 by John Doe.

def add(x, y):
    """Return the sum of two numbers."""
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    """Return the difference of two numbers."""
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    """Return the product of two numbers."""
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    """Return the quotient of two numbers."""
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y

# This is a class that represents a bank account.
class BankAccount:
    def __init__(self, balance=0):
        """Initialize a bank account with a balance."""
        self.balance = balance

    def deposit(self, amount):
        """Deposit money into the bank account."""
        self.balance += amount

    def withdraw(self, amount):
        """Withdraw money from the bank account."""
        if amount > self.balance:
            raise ValueError("Insufficient funds!")
        self.balance -= amount

    def get_balance(self):
        """Return the current balance of the bank account."""
        return self.balance

# This is a Python module that provides functions for calculating mathematical operations.
# The module was created in 2022 by John Doe.

def add(x, y):
    """
    Return the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    """
    Return the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    """
    Return the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of x and y.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(4, 5)
        20
    """
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    """
    Return the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The dividend.
        y (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of x and y.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If y is zero.

    Examples:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5.0
    """
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y

# This is a class that represents a bank account.
class BankAccount:
    """
    A class that represents a bank account.

    Attributes:
        balance (int or float): The current balance of the bank account.
    """

    def __init__(self, balance=0):
        """
        Initialize a bank account with a balance.

        Args:
            balance (int or float, optional): The initial balance. Defaults to 0.
        """
        self.balance = balance

    def deposit(self, amount):
        """
        Deposit money into the bank account.

        Args:
            amount (int or float): The amount to deposit.

        Examples:
            >>> account = BankAccount()
            >>> account.deposit(100)
            >>> account.get_balance()
            100
        """
        self.balance += amount

    def withdraw(self, amount):
        """
        Withdraw money from the bank account.

        Args:
            amount (int or float): The amount to withdraw.

        Raises:
            ValueError: If the amount exceeds the current balance.

        Examples:
            >>> account = BankAccount(100)
            >>> account.withdraw(50)
            >>> account.get_balance()
            50
        """
        if amount > self.balance:
            raise ValueError("Insufficient funds!")
        self.balance -= amount

    def get_balance(self):
        """
        Return the current balance of the bank account.

        Returns:
            int or float: The current balance.

        Examples:
            >>> account = BankAccount(100)
            >>> account.get_balance()
            100
        """
        return self.balance

# my_module.py
def add(a, b):
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    return a - b

class Calculator:
    def __init__(self, num1, num2):
        self.num1 = num1
        self.num2 = num2

    def multiply(self):
        return self.num1 * self.num2

    def divide(self):
        if self.num2!= 0:
            return self.num1 / self.num2
        else:
            raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")

# my_module.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return a - b

class Calculator:
    """
    A class used to perform mathematical operations.

    Attributes:
        num1 (int or float): The first number.
        num2 (int or float): The second number.
    """

    def __init__(self, num1, num2):
        """
        Initializes the Calculator object.

        Args:
            num1 (int or float): The first number.
            num2 (int or float): The second number.
        """
        self.num1 = num1
        self.num2 = num2

    def multiply(self):
        """
        Returns the product of the two numbers.

        Returns:
            int or float: The product of num1 and num2.

        Examples:
            >>> calc = Calculator(4, 5)
            >>> calc.multiply()
            20
        """
        return self.num1 * self.num2

    def divide(self):
        """
        Returns the quotient of the two numbers.

        Returns:
            int or float: The quotient of num1 and num2.

        Raises:
            ValueError: If num2 is zero.

        Examples:
            >>> calc = Calculator(10, 2)
            >>> calc.divide()
            5.0
        """
        if self.num2!= 0:
            return self.num1 / self.num2
        else:
            raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")

# my_module.py
"""
This module contains various utility functions and classes.

Functions:
    greet(name: str) -> str: Returns a personalized greeting message.
    add(a: int, b: int) -> int: Returns the sum of two integers.

Classes:
    Person: Represents a person with a name and age.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two integers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first integer.
        b (int): The second integer.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The name of the person.
        age (int): The age of the person.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."

# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Return a personalized greeting.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A personalized greeting message.

    Examples:
        >>> greet("John")
        'Hello, John!'
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Return the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add_numbers(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initialize a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.

        Attributes:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Return a greeting message.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.

        Examples:
            >>> person = Person("John", 30)
            >>> person.say_hello()
            'Hello, my name is John and I am 30 years old.'
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."

# my_other_module.py
def multiply_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Return the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The product of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply_numbers(2, 3)
        6
    """
    return a * b

def get_current_year() -> int:
    """
    Return the current year.

    Returns:
        int: The current year.

    Examples:
        >>> get_current_year()
        2024
    """
    from datetime import date
    return date.today().year

# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> str:
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    return a + b

class Person:
    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I'm {self.age} years old."
<END_TEXT>

# my_module.py
"""
This module contains various utility functions and classes.

Functions:
    greet(name: str) -> str: Returns a personalized greeting message.
    add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int: Adds two numbers and returns the result.

Classes:
    Person: Represents a person with a name and age.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Adds two numbers and returns the result.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The person's name.
        age (int): The person's age.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The person's name.
            age (int): The person's age.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I'm {self.age} years old."
<END_RESPONSE>

    return a + b

# my_module.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return a - b

def multiply(a, b):
    """
    Returns the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> multiply(4, 5)
        20
    """
    return a * b

def divide(a, b):
    """
    Returns the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The dividend.
        b (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of a and b.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If the divisor is zero.

    Examples:
        >>> divide(10, 2)
        5.0
    """
    if b == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return a / b

"""
This module contains various utility functions and classes.

Functions:
    greet(name: str) -> str: Returns a personalized greeting message.
    add(a: int, b: int) -> int: Returns the sum of two integers.

Classes:
    Person: Represents a person with a name and age.

    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two integers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first integer.
        b (int): The second integer.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The name of the person.
        age (int): The age of the person.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.

        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.

        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."

    """
    A simple calculator class.
    """

    def __init__(self):
        """
        Initializes the calculator.
        """
        pass

    def multiply(self, a, b):
        """
        Returns the product of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int): The first number.
            b (int): The second number.

        Returns:
            int: The product of a and b.

        return a * b

        """
        Returns the quotient of two numbers.

            a (int): The dividend.

# math_operations.py
def add(x, y):
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y

# math_operations.py
def add(x, y):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of x and y.
    """
    return x + y

def subtract(x, y):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of x and y.
    """
    return x - y

def multiply(x, y):
    """
    Returns the product of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The first number.
        y (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The product of x and y.
    """
    return x * y

def divide(x, y):
    """
    Returns the quotient of two numbers.

    Args:
        x (int or float): The dividend.
        y (int or float): The divisor.

    Returns:
        int or float: The quotient of x and y.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If y is zero.
    """
    if y == 0:
        raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero!")
    return x / y

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def farewell(name):
    """
    Returns a personalized farewell message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to bid farewell.

    Returns:
        str: A farewell message.
    """
    return f"Goodbye, {name}!"

# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Return a personalized greeting.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A personalized greeting message.

    Examples:
        >>> greet("John")
        'Hello, John!'
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Return the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add_numbers(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initialize a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.

        Attributes:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Return a greeting from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message from the person.

        Examples:
            >>> person = Person("Jane", 30)
            >>> person.say_hello()
            'Hello, my name is Jane and I\'m 30 years old.'
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I'm {self.age} years old."

# my_module.py
"""
This module contains functions and classes for various tasks.

Functions:
    greet(name: str) -> None: Prints a personalized greeting message.
    add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int: Returns the sum of two numbers.

Classes:
    Person: Represents a person with a name and age.
        Methods:
            say_hello() -> None: Prints a greeting message from the person.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> None:
    """
    Prints a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        None
    """
    print(f"Hello, {name}!")

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The name of the person.
        age (int): The age of the person.

    Methods:
        say_hello() -> None: Prints a greeting message from the person.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> None:
        """
        Prints a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            None
        """
        print(f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old.")


# my_other_module.py
"""
This module contains functions for calculating area and perimeter of a rectangle.

Functions:
    calculate_area(length: int, width: int) -> int: Returns the area of a rectangle.
    calculate_perimeter(length: int, width: int) -> int: Returns the perimeter of a rectangle.
"""

def calculate_area(length: int, width: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the area of a rectangle.

    Args:
        length (int): The length of the rectangle.
        width (int): The width of the rectangle.

    Returns:
        int: The area of the rectangle.
    """
    return length * width

def calculate_perimeter(length: int, width: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the perimeter of a rectangle.

    Args:
        length (int): The length of the rectangle.
        width (int): The width of the rectangle.

    Returns:
        int: The perimeter of the rectangle.
    """
    return 2 * (length + width)

While generating Python docstrings for the given modules and functions can be a useful tool for documentation and understanding code, it is essential to consider the potential limitations and flaws of this approach.

One major concern is that automated docstring generation may not always accurately capture the nuances and complexities of the code. For instance, the generated docstrings may not fully convey the intent and context of the functions and modules, potentially leading to misunderstandings or misuses.

Moreover, relying solely on automated docstring generation may lead to a lack of human oversight and review, which is crucial for ensuring the accuracy and quality of the documentation. This could result in outdated, incomplete, or incorrect documentation, ultimately defeating the purpose of having docstrings in the first place.

Here is an example of how the code could be modified to include docstrings, but it is crucial to review and refine these docstrings to ensure they accurately reflect the code's functionality:

```python
# my_module.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The difference of a and b.
    """
    return a - b

class Calculator:
    """
    A simple calculator class.
    """

    def __init__(self):
        """
        Initializes the calculator.
        """
        pass

    def multiply(self, a, b):
        """
        Returns the product of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int): The first number.
            b (int): The second number.

        Returns:
            int: The product of a and b.
        """
        return a * b

    def divide(self, a, b):
        """
        Returns the quotient of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int): The dividend.
            b (int): The divisor.

        Returns:
            float: The quotient of a and b.

        Raises:
            ValueError: If the divisor is zero.
        """
        if b == 0:
            raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
        return a / b
```

In conclusion, while automated docstring generation can be a useful tool, it is crucial to approach this task with a critical eye, recognizing both the benefits and limitations of this approach. By combining automated generation with human review and refinement, we can create high-quality documentation that accurately reflects the code's functionality and intent.

    add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int: Returns the sum of two numbers.

Classes:
    Person: Represents a person with a name and age.
"""

def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add_numbers(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    Represents a person with a name and age.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The name of the person.
        age (int): The age of the person.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The name of the person.
            age (int): The age of the person.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."

    Returns:
        int: The sum of the numbers.
    """

# my_module.py
def greet(name: str) -> str:
    """
    Returns a personalized greeting message.

    Args:
        name (str): The name of the person to greet.

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

def add(a: int, b: int) -> int:
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

class Person:
    """
    A class representing a person.

    Attributes:
        name (str): The person's name.
        age (int): The person's age.
    """

    def __init__(self, name: str, age: int):
        """
        Initializes a Person object.

        Args:
            name (str): The person's name.
            age (int): The person's age.
        """
        self.name = name
        self.age = age

    def say_hello(self) -> str:
        """
        Returns a greeting message from the person.

        Returns:
            str: A greeting message.
        """
        return f"Hello, my name is {self.name} and I am {self.age} years old."

Classes:

    Returns:
        str: A greeting message.
    """
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int): The first number.
        b (int): The second number.

    Returns:
        int: The sum of a and b.
    """
    return a + b

        self.age = age

# my_module.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return a - b

class Calculator:
    """
    A simple calculator class.

    Attributes:
        None

    Methods:
        multiply(a, b): Returns the product of two numbers.
        divide(a, b): Returns the quotient of two numbers.
    """

    def __init__(self):
        """
        Initializes the Calculator object.

        Args:
            None

        Returns:
            None
        """
        pass

    def multiply(self, a, b):
        """
        Returns the product of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int or float): The first number.
            b (int or float): The second number.

        Returns:
            int or float: The product of a and b.

        Examples:
            >>> calc = Calculator()
            >>> calc.multiply(4, 5)
            20
        """
        return a * b

    def divide(self, a, b):
        """
        Returns the quotient of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int or float): The dividend.
            b (int or float): The divisor.

        Returns:
            int or float: The quotient of a and b.

        Raises:
            ValueError: If the divisor is zero.

        Examples:
            >>> calc = Calculator()
            >>> calc.divide(10, 2)
            5.0
        """
        if b == 0:
            raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
        return a / b

# my_module.py
def add(a, b):
    """
    Returns the sum of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The sum of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> add(2, 3)
        5
    """
    return a + b

def subtract(a, b):
    """
    Returns the difference of two numbers.

    Args:
        a (int or float): The first number.
        b (int or float): The second number.

    Returns:
        int or float: The difference of a and b.

    Examples:
        >>> subtract(5, 3)
        2
    """
    return a - b

class Calculator:
    """
    A simple calculator class.

    Attributes:
        None

    Methods:
        multiply(a, b): Returns the product of two numbers.
        divide(a, b): Returns the quotient of two numbers.
    """

    def __init__(self):
        """
        Initializes the Calculator object.

        Args:
            None

        Returns:
            None
        """
        pass

    def multiply(self, a, b):
        """
        Returns the product of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int or float): The first number.
            b (int or float): The second number.

        Returns:
            int or float: The product of a and b.

        Examples:
            >>> calculator = Calculator()
            >>> calculator.multiply(4, 5)
            20
        """
        return a * b

    def divide(self, a, b):
        """
        Returns the quotient of two numbers.

        Args:
            a (int or float): The dividend.
            b (int or float): The divisor.

        Returns:
            int or float: The quotient of a and b.

        Raises:
            ValueError: If the divisor is zero.

        Examples:
            >>> calculator = Calculator()
            >>> calculator.divide(10, 2)
            5.0
        """
        if b == 0:
            raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero")
        return a / b

def calculate_area(length, width):
    return length * width

def calculate_perimeter(length, width):
    return 2 * (length + width)

class Rectangle:
    def __init__(self, length, width):
        self.length = length
        self.width = width

    def area(self):
        return calculate_area(self.length, self.width)

    def perimeter(self):
        return calculate_perimeter(self.length, self.width)

<BEGIN_RESPONSE> 
def calculate_area(length, width):
    """
    Calculate the area of a rectangle.

    Args:
        length (float): The length of the rectangle.
        width (float): The width of the rectangle.

    Returns:
        float: The area of the rectangle.
    """
    return length * width

def calculate_perimeter(length, width):
    """
    Calculate the perimeter of a rectangle.

    Args:
        length (float): The length of the rectangle.
        width (float): The width of the rectangle.

    Returns:
        float: The perimeter of the rectangle.
    """
    return 2 * (length + width)

class Rectangle:
    """
    A class representing a rectangle.

    Attributes:
        length (float): The length of the rectangle.
        width (float): The width of the rectangle.
    """

    def __init__(self, length, width):
        """
        Initialize a Rectangle object.

        Args:
            length (float): The length of the rectangle.
            width (float): The width of the rectangle.
        """
        self.length = length
        self.width = width

    def area(self):
        """
        Calculate the area of the rectangle.

        Returns:
            float: The area of the rectangle.
        """
        return calculate_area(self.length, self.width)

    def perimeter(self):
        """
        Calculate the perimeter of the rectangle.

        Returns:
            float: The perimeter of the rectangle.
        """
        return calculate_perimeter(self.length, self.width)
